2:28:1771:0:14:72:533:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:A:The Structure of State Corporate Taxation and its Impact on State Tax Revenues and Economic 
2:29:1862:14:14:72:111:686:12:Times:12:Times:A:Activity
2:30:1870:14:14:72:299:672:12:Times:12:Times:A:Juan Carlos Suárez Serrato and Owen M. Zidar
2:31:1914:14:14:72:234:658:12:Times:12:Times:A:NBER Working Paper No. 23653
2:32:1942:14:14:72:228:644:12:Times:12:g_d0_f3:A:August 2017, Revised July 2018

2:34:1993:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:35:2001:28:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:A:This  paper  documents  facts  about  the  state  corporate  tax  structure  |  tax  rates,  base  rules,  and 
2:36:2112:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:A:credits | and investigates its consequences for state tax revenue and economic activity. We present 
2:37:2211:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:A:three  main findings.  First,  tax  base  rules  and  credits  explain  more  of  the  variation  in  state 
2:38:2318:14:14:72:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:A:corporate  tax  revenues than  tax  rates  do.  Second,  although  states  typically  do  not  offset  tax  rate 
2:39:2430:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:A:changes  with  base  and  credit changes,  the  effects  of  tax  rate  changes  on  tax  revenue  and 
2:40:2532:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:A:economic  activity  depend  on  the  breadth of  the  base.  Third,  as  states  have  narrowed  their  tax 
2:41:2639:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:A:bases,  the  relationship  between  tax  rates  and  tax revenues  has  diminished.  Overall,  changes  in 
2:42:2745:14:14:72:546:476:12:Times:12:Times:A:state tax bases have made the state corporate tax system more favorable for corporations and are 
2:43:2841:14:42:72:430:462:12:Times:12:Times:A:reducing the extent to which tax rate increases raise corporate tax revenue.
2:44:2916:42:14:72:202:420:12:Times:12:Times:A:Juan Carlos Suárez Serrato
2:45:2942:14:14:72:198:406:12:Times:12:Times:A:Department of Economics
2:46:2965:14:14:72:152:392:12:Times:12:Times:A:Duke University
2:47:2980:14:14:72:213:378:12:Times:12:Times:A:213 Social Sciences Building
2:48:3008:14:14:72:125:364:12:Times:12:Times:A:Box 90097
2:49:3017:14:14:72:167:350:12:Times:12:Times:A:Durham, NC 27708
2:50:3033:14:14:72:124:336:12:Times:12:Times:A:and NBER
2:51:3041:14:28:72:155:322:12:Times:12:Times:A:jc@jcsuarez.com
2:52:3056:28:14:72:146:294:12:Times:12:Times:A:Owen M. Zidar
2:53:3069:14:14:72:335:280:12:Times:12:Times:A:Department of Economics & Woodrow Wilson School
2:54:3116:14:14:72:172:266:12:Times:12:Times:A:Princeton University
2:55:3136:14:14:72:251:252:12:Times:12:Times:A:237 Julis Romo Rabinowitz Building
2:56:3170:14:14:72:170:238:12:Times:12:Times:A:Princeton, NJ 08544
2:57:3189:14:14:72:124:224:12:Times:12:Times:A:and NBER

3:59:3217:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:How states tax businesses has received renewed interest in both academic and policy circles.  Recent work on
3:60:3325:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:state corporate tax rates has investigated their impacts on income growth, employment, and business location.1
3:61:3435:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:However, state policymakers compete to attract businesses not only by changing tax rates, but also by changing
3:62:3545:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the tax base to enhance several investment incentives, loss provisions, and enforcement mechanisms.2There
3:63:3650:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:is  a  lack  of  basic  facts  about  the  state  corporate  tax  structure,  its  evolution  over  recent  years,  and  how  it
3:64:3778:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:impacts tax revenue and economic activity.  This paper describes the state corporate tax structure, documents
3:65:3887:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:how it has changed over time, and investigates the consequences of these changes for state tax collections and
3:66:3997:18:18:63:141:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:economic activity.
3:67:4015:18:18:78:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Our analysis proceeds in four steps.  We first describe recent trends in state corporate tax structure.3While
3:68:4124:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:average state corporate tax rates have remained relatively stable, state corporate tax revenues as a share of
3:69:4233:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:economic  activity  have  declined  substantially.   Some  of  this  decline  is  due  to  other  factors  (e.g.,  the  rise  of
3:70:4361:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:pass-throughs (Cooper et al., 2016) and corporate losses (Auerbach and Poterba, 1987)),  but we show that
3:71:4466:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax base and credit changes have substantial impacts on state corporate tax collections.  Tax base and credit
3:72:4575:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes are much more frequent than tax rate changes.  Contrary to the view that state tax rate changes are
3:73:4682:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:often accompanied by offsetting changes in the tax base, we find that the vast majority of tax base changes
3:74:4789:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:are not associated with tax rate changes.  Some provisions, such as R&D credits, investment tax credits, and
3:75:4897:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:loss carryforward rules, have become more favorable for corporations while others (e.g., throwback rules and
3:76:5005:18:18:63:273:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:combined reporting) have lead to broader bases.
3:77:5052:18:18:78:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Second, we estimate the importance of each of these tax base rules for state corporate tax collections from
3:78:5159:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:1980 and 2010.  We perform analysis of variance decompositions every five years and document the importance
3:79:5266:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of tax base rules, relative to tax rates, in explaining the variation in corporate tax revenue across states and
3:80:5378:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:over time.  Overall, tax base components account for the majority of the explained variation in tax revenues.
3:81:5487:18:18:63:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This result remains relatively stable throughout most of our sample, with only a slight increase in the fraction
3:82:5599:18:18:63:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:explained by tax rates in 2010.  The importance of different tax base components in explaining tax revenues has
3:83:5710:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:evolved over our sample.  In particular, sales apportionment weights and loss carryback provisions have waned
3:84:5819:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in  importance,  while  franchise  taxes,  different  depreciation  rules,  and  interactions  with  federal  tax  policies,
3:85:5943:18:17:63:542:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:such as adopting the federal tax base or allowing for the deductibility of federal taxes,  have increased their
3:86:6054:17:18:63:183:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:share of explained variance.
3:87:6082:18:18:78:542:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Third, we analyze how tax base provisions affect the relationship between state tax rates and two outcomes:
3:88:6189:18:18:63:542:204:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:state corporate tax revenue and state GDP. This analysis has two parts.  We first explore the degree to which
3:89:6298:18:18:63:542:186:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f4:B:controlling for these tax base provisionsaffects the relationship between tax rates and revenue and GDP. We
3:90:6405:18:15:63:542:168:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:find that, while tax base controls explain a large portion of the variation in revenues, the relationships between
3:91:6519:15:12:77:526:153:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:1Recent papers includeHeider and Ljungqvist(2015),Giroud and Rauh(2015),Su ́arez Serrato and Zidar(2016),Fajgel-
3:92:6631:12:7:63:335:141:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:baum et al.(2015),Ohrn(2016), andLjungqvist and Smolyansky(2014).
3:93:6696:7:12:77:514:134:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:2These tax base rules are important determinants of measures of state business climate indexes (e.g.,Tax Foundation
3:94:6811:12:10:63:528:122:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:(2016)).ALEC(2014) reports that 14 states changed taxes in 2014 with many of the changes affecting both tax rates as well
3:95:6932:10:9:63:81:112:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:as tax base determinants.3
3:96:6958:9:10:81:536:103:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:The fifteen determinants of the corporate income tax structure that we analyze include tax credits, such as the investment
3:97:7080:10:9:63:542:93:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:tax credit and the R&D tax credit.  For simplicity, we refer to these credits as determinants of the tax base, along with our other
3:98:7211:9:0:63:133:84:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:tax base measures.
4:99:7230:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax rates and our outcomes of interest are not fundamentally affected by controlling for these tax base measures.
4:100:7343:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This result may be due to the lack of a temporal coincidence between changes to tax rates and determinants
4:101:7449:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of the tax base.  However, even if tax base and rate changes do not occur at the same time, the tax base can
4:102:7557:18:18:63:237:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:influence the effects of tax rate changes.
4:103:7599:18:18:78:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:We then explore the extent to whichinteractions between the tax base and tax ratesinduce heterogeneous
4:104:7701:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:effects  of  state  corporate  tax  rate  changes.   Intuitively,  when  the  tax  base  is  narrow,  a  tax  rate  increase
4:105:7825:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:mechanically raises less revenue since taxable income is a smaller portion of overall income.  In addition, tax
4:106:7936:18:18:63:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes have smaller incentive effects, so the behavioral responses to tax rate increases are likely attenuated.
4:107:8048:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Empirically, we first confirm that states with narrower tax bases collect less revenue from marginal increases
4:108:8158:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in tax rates.  The main finding is about tax-base-driven heterogeneity in the time series.  While some states
4:109:8267:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:have broadened the base (e.g., Michigan, Ohio, Illinois), we observe narrower tax bases on average over the last
4:110:8379:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:thirty years.  These trends in state tax bases over time have made the state corporate tax system more generous
4:111:8490:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:towards corporations, and are reducing the extent to which increases in tax rates raise corporate tax revenue.
4:112:8600:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:In addition, we find that including interactions between the state tax base and state tax rates also increases
4:113:8710:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the estimate of the average treatment effect (ATE) of state corporate tax rate changes on state corporate tax
4:114:8819:18:18:63:103:455:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:revenue.4
4:115:8828:18:18:78:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:We conclude by investigating the implications of these results for revenue-maximizing-state-tax rates and
4:116:8933:18:18:63:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for the claim that state corporate tax rate cuts pay for themselves.5We estimate a regression in which tax rates
4:117:9045:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:have linear (β0) and quadratic (δ0) effects on tax revenue.  The revenue-maximizing-state-corporate-tax rate
4:118:9153:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:equals the ratio of these effects:β0−2δ0.  The estimate of the quadratic effect (ˆδ0), which measures decreasing
4:119:9265:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:returns  from  tax  rate  increases,  is  not  substantially  larger  than  the  linear  effect  (ˆβ0).   Our  point  estimates
4:120:9392:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:imply that the tax rate that maximizes state corporate tax revenue is close to 30 percent.  InSu ́arez Serrato
4:121:9502:18:18:63:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and Zidar(2016), we note that state corporate taxes may have fiscal externalities and may affect tax revenue
4:122:9610:18:18:63:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:from sales and personal income taxes.  Even when we allow for this externality by considering total state tax
4:123:9719:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenue instead of only corporate tax revenue, our estimates imply a total-state-tax-revenue-maximizing rate
4:124:9827:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of close to 10%.  Since the estimated revenue-maximizing rate is greater than the majority of state corporate
4:125:9936:18:17:63:394:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax rates, we reject the hypothesis that tax cuts tend to pay for themselves.
4:126:10013:17:18:78:542:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:This paper contributes to three literatures.  First, relative to recent work on the effects of changes in state
4:127:10124:18:18:63:542:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:business tax rates on economic activity (Heider and Ljungqvist(2015),Giroud and Rauh(2015),Su ́arez Serrato
4:128:10231:18:18:63:543:204:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and Zidar(2016),Fajgelbaum et al.(2015),Ohrn(2016), andLjungqvist and Smolyansky(2014)), we explore
4:129:10330:18:18:63:542:186:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:how the relationships between tax rates and revenues and economic activity depend on the structure of the
4:130:10435:18:18:63:542:168:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax system.  A contribution of this paper is the collection and description of a comprehensive set of
4:131:10546:18:15:63:542:150:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:variables that describe the structure of the corporate tax system across all U.S. states since 1980, which we
4:132:10655:15:12:77:535:135:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:4As is well known (Wooldridge,2005;Gibbons, Su ́arez Serrato and Urbancic,2014), in the presence of heterogeneous treat-
4:133:10775:12:10:63:541:123:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:ment effects, regressions that control for the drivers of heterogeneity estimate a weighted-average of the heterogeneous treatment
4:134:10905:10:9:63:539:113:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:effects that may not be a consistent estimate of the average treatment effect.  In this context, the source of heterogeneous effects
4:135:11037:9:7:63:326:104:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:is the tax base.  We discuss treatment effect heterogeneity in Section5.
4:136:11109:7:12:77:528:97:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:5See, for instance, claims by Sam Brownback (Mclean,2017), Thom Tillis (The News & Observer Editorial Board,2017),
4:137:11223:12:10:63:524:85:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:and Mitt Romney (Romney, 2010) for the cases of Kansas, North Carolina, and Massachusetts, respectively, and Rand Paul
4:138:11341:10:0:63:263:75:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:(Kessler,2015) for a similar claim at the federal level.
5:139:11398:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:hope will aid future researchers in this literature.  In a contemporaneous contribution, Bartik (2017) simulates
5:140:11510:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the tax consequences of locating a new plant in 32 states and 45 industries that cover roughly 90 percent of
5:141:11618:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:U.S.  economic  activity  since  1990.   These  simulations  are  highly  detailed  and  capture  complex  interactions
5:142:11737:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:between  several  rules.   We  view  this  paper  as  highly  complementary  to  ours,  which  takes  a  reduced-form
5:143:11854:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:empirical  approach.   Specifically,  we  do  not  conduct  similar  simulations  at  the  plant  level,  but  do  variance
5:144:11977:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:decompositions of observed state corporate tax revenue as a share of state GDP to understand the quantitative
5:145:12086:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:importance of different base provisions for state tax revenue.  Bartik (2017) also documents several facts about
5:146:12198:18:18:63:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes in incentives and finds that business incentives are large,  vary substantially across states,  and have
5:147:12310:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:become increasingly generous.  Consistent with these results, we document substantial variation across states
5:148:12419:18:18:63:445:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and a general narrowing of the base on average in the full panel of 50 states since 1980.
5:149:12508:18:18:78:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Second, this paper is also related to a set of papers that explore whether the tax base affects the relationship
5:150:12620:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:between  corporate  tax  rates  and  corporate  income  tax  revenues.   In  particular,Clausing(2007),Devereux
5:151:12731:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:(2007),  andKawano  and  Slemrod(2015)  study  this  relationship  across  29  OECD  member  countries,  and
5:152:12839:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Dahlby  and  Ferede(2012)  perform  a  similar  analysis  across  Canadian  provinces.   We  followKawano  and
5:153:12949:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Slemrod(2015) by collecting a comprehensive set of variables that describe the breadth of the tax base and by
5:154:13058:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:controlling for this tax base vector in our estimations.  In contrast toKawano and Slemrod(2015), who focus
5:155:13165:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:on the international corporate tax structure, we find that state tax rate changes are not often offset by base
5:156:13275:18:18:63:147:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and credit changes.
5:157:13294:18:18:78:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Finally, we find that the relationship between state tax rates and economic activity depends on the structure
5:158:13403:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of the tax base.  This point is related to work byKopczuk(2005),  who finds that the elasticity of reported
5:159:13510:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:taxable income for individuals depends on the availability of deductions.  In our setting, this dependence on the
5:160:13623:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax base is important for revenue forecasts and assessments of the incidence and efficiency of state corporate
5:161:13733:18:18:63:102:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:taxation.
5:162:13742:18:18:78:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:The paper is organized as follows.  Section1 describes the dataset of tax base determinants, and Section2
5:163:13847:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:describes trends in the structure of the state corporate tax system.  Section3 performs the variance decompo-
5:164:13956:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:sition analysis, and Section4 explores the effects of controlling for tax base determinants on various outcomes
5:165:14067:18:17:63:542:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of economic interest.  Section5 explores tax-base-driven treatment effect heterogeneity across states and over
5:166:14177:17:18:63:543:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:time, Section6 analyzes the revenue-maximizing-tax rate, and Section7 concludes with a discussion of policy
5:167:14284:18:42:63:118:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:implications.
5:168:14297:42:28:63:413:180:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:1    Measuring the State Corporate Tax Structure
5:169:14345:28:18:63:542:152:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We  use  fifteen  measures  of  the  corporate  tax  base  for  the  main  analysis  in  the  paper.   Details  on  each  of
5:170:14469:18:18:63:542:134:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the variables, sources, and coverage are available in AppendixA.6The following variables comprise our state-
5:171:14577:18:15:63:542:116:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:year panel dataset of tax base and credit components:  an indicator of having throwback rules, an indicator of
5:172:14687:15:12:77:524:101:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:6Most of the data used in this paper were digitized from a variety of sources includingCCH State Tax Handbook(1980-
5:173:14802:12:9:63:540:89:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:2010) andCSG Book of the State(1976-2011), but we also rely on data collected and generously provided byChirinko and Wil-
5:174:14923:9:10:63:538:80:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:son(2008),Wilson(2009), andBernthal et al.(2012).  Unless otherwise indicated, we exclude the District of Columbia from the
5:175:15046:10:0:63:94:70:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:analysis.
6:176:15056:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:having combined reporting rules, investment tax credit rates, research and development (R&D) tax credit rates,
6:177:15166:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:an indicator for whether the R&D tax credit applies to an incremental base that is a moving average of past
6:178:15273:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:expenditures, an indicator for whether the R&D tax credit applies to an incremental base that is fixed on a level
6:179:15386:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of past expenditures, the number of years for loss carryback, number of years for loss carryforward, an indicator
6:180:15499:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for franchise taxes, an indicator for federal income tax deductibility, an indicator for federal income tax base as
6:181:15614:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the state tax base, an indicator for follows federal accelerated depreciation, an indicator for follows accelerated
6:182:15729:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:cost recovery system (MACRS) depreciation,  an indicator for federal bonus depreciation,  and corporate tax
6:183:15836:18:18:63:165:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:apportionment weights.
6:184:15858:18:18:78:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Most of the variables are indicators of whether a state allows a particular policy.  Throwback and combined
6:185:15965:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:reporting rules come fromBernthal et al.(2012) and describe whether a state requires a unitary business to
6:186:16071:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:submit combined reporting and, in the case of throwback rules, whether a state eliminates “nowhere income”
6:187:16177:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:that would be untaxed by either the state with the corporation’s nexus or the state in which the relevant sales
6:188:16288:17:18:63:139:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:were being made.
6:189:16304:18:18:78:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Data on state investment tax credits and R&D tax credits come fromChirinko and Wilson(2008),  and
6:190:16401:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Wilson(2009)  provides  the  rate  of  each  of  these  credits.   For  the  R&D  credit,  we  use  the  statutory  credit
6:191:16523:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:rate adjusted for recapture and type of credit.  States vary in how they implement R&D tax credits.  States
6:192:16630:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:determine whether the R&D tax credit applies to all qualified expenditures, or whether the base is incremental
6:193:16740:18:18:63:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:based on previous expenditures.  In addition, the basis of previous expenditures may be fixed in time or may
6:194:16848:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:be a moving average of recent activity.  We control for two indicators for whether the base is incremental and
6:195:16958:18:18:63:354:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:fixed, or whether it is incremental and based on a moving average.
6:196:17024:18:18:78:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Loss rules specify the number of years that a corporation may carry back net operating loss prior to the
6:197:17128:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:loss as well as the number of years a corporation may carry forward any excess loss following the loss year.  The
6:198:17241:18:18:63:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation indicators describe whether a state conforms to federal depreciation rules and adopts federal bonus
6:199:17353:18:18:63:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation  policies  that  accelerate  investment  incentives  (seeZwick  and  Mahon(2017)  for  policy  details).
6:200:17470:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Finally, we use apportionment weights for payroll, property, and sales that were digitized fromCSG Book of
6:201:17576:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the State(1976-2011).  These weights determine the share of national profits of multi-state firms that is taxable
6:202:17689:18:17:63:527:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in a given state (see section IV.B ofSu ́arez Serrato and Zidar(2016) for policy details on apportionment).
6:203:17796:17:18:78:542:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:In addition to our data on tax base measures,  we use a few other data sources in the analysis.  We use
6:204:17899:18:18:63:542:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:statutory state corporate income tax rates fromCSG Book of the State(1976-2011), top statutory personal
6:205:18002:18:18:63:542:204:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:income tax rate from NBER TAXSIM, GDP from theU.S. Bureau of Economic Analysis(1967-2016), and tax
6:206:18100:18:18:63:358:186:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:revenue data from theU.S. Department of Commerce(1942-2012).7
6:207:18161:18:18:78:542:168:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Table1 provides summary statistics of our main base measures.  In the pooled sample from 1980 to 2010,
6:208:18263:18:18:63:542:150:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:roughly  half  of  the  states  had  throwback  rules  and  franchise  taxes.   Most  used  federal  income  as  the  state
6:209:18386:18:18:63:542:132:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax  base  and  followed  accelerated  depreciation  schedules  (although  some  states  stopped  allowing  for  bonus
6:210:18504:18:15:63:542:114:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:depreciation for budgetary reasons).  Roughly a quarter of states in the pooled sample used combined reporting
6:211:18614:15:13:77:539:99:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:F:7See Feenberg and Coutts(1993) for more details on NBER TAXSIM. In robustness analysis, we also use use annual payroll
6:212:18732:13:9:63:538:86:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:fromCounty Business Patterns(2010), and, for a subset of states and year, additional base controls fromBartik(2017), such as
6:213:18856:9:0:63:224:77:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:property taxes and job creation tax credits.
7:214:18901:0:42:63:312:724:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:rules, although this share has been increasing over time.8
7:215:18959:42:28:63:501:682:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:2    Trends and Changes in the State Corporate Tax Structure
7:216:19019:28:18:63:543:654:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:The structure of state corporate taxation varies widely across states and over time.  Figure1 shows that the
7:217:19127:18:18:63:542:636:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:statutory corporate income tax rate varies between 0 and 12%.  Five states (Nevada,  South Dakota,  Texas,
7:218:19233:18:18:63:542:618:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Washington,  and  Wyoming)  currently  have  no  taxes  on  corporate  income.   As  of  2012,  another  five  states
7:219:19350:18:18:63:542:600:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:(Alaska, Illinois, Iowa, Minnesota, and Pennsylvania) had tax rates above 9%.  Figure1 shows that over the
7:220:19456:18:18:63:542:582:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:past few decades,  very modest increases in the state corporate tax rate distribution across states have been
7:221:19565:18:18:63:542:564:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:accompanied by substantial declines in state corporate tax revenue as a share of economic activity.  Panel A of
7:222:19676:18:18:63:542:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Figure2 shows this pattern directly – average state corporate tax rates are quite stable, but the average state
7:223:19787:18:17:63:542:528:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax revenue as a share of GDP has declined nearly 40%.  While part of this decline arises from the
7:224:19895:17:18:63:542:511:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:shift away from the traditional corporate form (Cooper et al.(2016)), losses and other factors (Auerbach and
7:225:20003:18:18:63:443:493:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:Poterba(1987)), part of this decline is due to changes in the state corporate tax base.9
7:226:20091:18:18:78:542:475:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Table2 describes the number of changes to each of our tax base measures.  This table shows that there
7:227:20192:18:18:63:542:457:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:are more changes categorized as tax base narrowing than broadening, which suggests that an aggregate trend
7:228:20298:18:18:63:543:439:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:towards narrower bases is partly responsible for the patterns in Figures1–2.  Of these changes, the increase
7:229:20406:18:18:63:542:421:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in the number of years allowed for carrying losses forward and the increased reliance on sales as a factor for
7:230:20516:18:18:63:372:403:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:apportionment are the most frequently reformed measures in our data.
7:231:20584:18:18:78:542:385:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Table3 compares changes in the tax base with changes in the tax rate.  As the resurgent literature studying
7:232:20691:18:18:63:542:367:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the effects of state corporate taxes on economic activity has noted, there have been a considerable number of
7:233:20800:18:18:63:542:349:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes to states’ tax rates.  This table shows that states have decreased rates in 70 occasions, while increasing
7:234:20914:18:18:63:542:331:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:rates 103 times, for a total of 173 changes.  However, this considerable policy activity pales in comparison to
7:235:21025:18:18:63:542:313:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes to the states’ tax bases.  Table3 shows that states have adopted changes that narrow the tax base in
7:236:21133:18:18:63:440:295:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:283 occasions, while increasing the base 163 times, for a total of 446 tax base changes.
7:237:21221:18:18:78:542:277:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:A widespread belief among economists and policy analysts is that increases in tax rates have relatively small
7:238:21330:18:17:63:542:259:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:effects on firms’ tax obligations, since legislatures often change tax rates and tax bases simultaneously.10In
7:239:21440:17:18:63:542:242:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:particular, if tax increases are accompanied by the narrowing of tax bases, firms’ effective tax rates will be less
7:240:21555:18:18:63:542:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:susceptible to changes in the statutory rate.  Panel B of Figure2 shows for each year the number of states that
7:241:21666:18:18:63:542:206:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:change their corporate tax rates and base provisions.  Most points fall below the red 45 degree line, illustrating
7:242:21780:18:15:63:534:188:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:that in almost all years in which states change their tax base, most of them do not change their tax rates.11
7:243:21889:15:12:77:541:173:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:F:8Panel B in Table1 provides summary statistics for the cross section of states in 2010 and shows that roughly half the states
7:244:22014:12:10:63:527:161:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:had combined reporting in 2010.  Appendix TableA1provides summary stats of the additionalBartik(2017) controls for the
7:245:22132:10:9:63:81:151:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:subset of states and years for which these data are available.9
7:246:22195:9:10:81:534:142:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:Ideally, one could decompose the importance of these different channels as inAuerbach and Poterba(1987).  However, the
7:247:22313:10:9:63:538:132:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:necessary state level inputs for this exercise are not publicly available.  SeeBartik(2017) for a detailed industry-state level anal-
7:248:22446:9:7:63:216:123:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:ysis of business tax incentives since 1990.
7:249:22489:7:12:73:539:116:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:F:10This belief is supported by cross-country studies, as inDevereux and Sørensen(2006) andKawano and Slemrod(2015).  At
7:250:22607:12:10:63:535:104:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:the subnational level, however, other authors have noted cases where the tax base is set at the federal level, while the tax rates
7:251:22737:10:9:63:80:94:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:are set at the sub-national level (Fuest, Peichl and Siegloch,2018).11
7:252:22807:9:10:81:523:85:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:Appendix FigureA1shows that this finding is also consistent in recent years and states that coincide with the analysis
7:253:22925:10:0:63:154:75:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:sample inBartik(2017).
8:254:22948:0:18:78:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Table 3provides additional evidence that state tax rates and tax bases are not typically temporally related,
8:255:23056:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:by  showing  the  number  of  times  that  states  changed  rates  and  tax  bases.   This  table  shows  that  in  most
8:256:23176:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:occasions  (43  out  of  70)  when  states  lowered  tax  rates,  these  changes  were  not  accompanied  by  a  tax  base
8:257:23298:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:change.  Similarly, when states increased tax rates, there were relatively few occasions when states also changed
8:258:23411:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the  tax  base  (only  9  out  of  103).   Conversely,  Table3  also  finds  that  when  states  changed  tax  bases,  these
8:259:23535:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes were very seldom accompanied by changes in the tax rates (23 out of 283 for base-narrowing changes,
8:260:23642:18:18:63:280:616:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:and 22 out of 163 for base-broadening changes).12
8:261:23691:18:18:78:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Table4 formalizes this point by presenting probit estimates of the likelihood of a coincidence in base and
8:262:23797:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:rate changes.  The first panel estimates the probability of a change in tax base as a function of a rate change.
8:263:23909:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This panel shows that changes in tax rates are not predictive of changes in tax bases, and that this pattern is
8:264:24020:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:robust to splitting the dependent variable into base-narrowing and broadening events.  Panel B estimates the
8:265:24128:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:converse relation using changes in tax bases to predict changes in tax rates.  In particular, when we estimate
8:266:24238:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the  likelihood  of  a  tax  increase,  we  observe  that  there  is  no  statistical  relation  with  a  state  also  narrowing
8:267:24366:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the tax base.  We only find a modest correlation between the likelihood of a tax change and a broadening of
8:268:24473:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the base.  The third column shows this result is driven by tax decreases and base broadenings.  However, it is
8:269:24583:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:sensitive to a few number of observations.13These results contrast with those ofKawano and Slemrod(2015),
8:270:24688:18:18:63:532:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:who estimate similar models for OECD countries and find statistically significant relations in all categories.
8:271:24798:18:18:78:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:We now describe  trends in  specific  tax base  and  credit provisions.   Figure3 shows  how  tax  credits,  loss
8:272:24911:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:rules, other base provisions and apportionment weights have evolved over time.  Panel A of Figure3 shows that
8:273:25020:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax credits, especially R&D credits, have become much more generous.  Panel B shows that loss carryforward
8:274:25126:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:provisions have become more favorable, and loss carryback provisions have remained relatively stable.  Figure
8:275:25235:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:4 shows how the distributions of many of these provisions have tended to become more generous over the past
8:276:25342:18:18:63:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:few decades.  In 1980, research and development credits were rare.  Beginning in 1990, some states introduced
8:277:25451:18:18:63:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:credits, but the vast majority of these were small – below 5%.  R&D tax credits have become more common in
8:278:25557:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the twenty-first century.  Many states have increased the size of the credit; as of 2010, a large share of states
8:279:25670:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:offer credits even more generous than the most generous provisions in 1990.  However, the generosity of these
8:280:25779:18:17:63:542:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:credits has been reduced by adoption of rules that limit R&D tax credits to incremental expenditures.  The data
8:281:25890:17:18:63:542:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:reveal similar patterns for the investment tax credit and loss carryforward provisions, which have on aggregate
8:282:26001:18:18:63:291:222:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:changed with the result of narrowing the tax base.14
8:283:26053:18:18:78:542:204:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Panel C of Figure3 shows that states have continued to narrow their base by increasing the apportionment
8:284:26157:18:18:63:542:186:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:weight on sales, and decreasing the weights on property and payroll.  In 1980, the majority of states placed
8:285:26265:18:18:63:542:168:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:less than half of the apportionment weight on sales.  This share declined steadily until 2010, leaving only 12
8:286:26375:18:18:63:542:150:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:states with sales apportionment shares below 50%.  Figure4 depicts this shift and the implications for the sales
8:287:26487:18:18:63:542:132:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:apportioned corporate tax rate, which is the product of the statutory corporate tax rate and the sales weight.
8:288:26597:18:15:63:542:114:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Given the secular decline in payroll and property weights, it is not surprising that the range of this distribution
8:289:26712:15:9:73:539:99:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:F:12Appendix TableA3provides more detail by describing the co-movement of tax rates and each individual tax base measure.
8:290:26831:9:13:73:522:90:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:13In particular, the adoption of throwback rules in 2007 by a small number of states is responsible for this result.  In Ap-
8:291:26955:13:9:63:80:77:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:pendix TableA4we show that this result is not robust to ignoring these changes.14
8:292:27036:9:0:81:487:68:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:Appendix FiguresA5–A19provide additional detail behind changes in individual tax base measures by state.
9:293:27141:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:is more compressed than the distribution of sales-apportioned corporate rate.  However, it is striking that the
9:294:27252:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:distribution of the sales-apportioned corporate rate is skewed to the right and has, if anything, become more
9:295:27361:18:18:63:526:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:dispersed in recent years by increasing the density of states with higher sales-apportioned corporate rates.
9:296:27469:18:18:78:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:In contrast, other dimensions of the tax base have expanded over the past few decades.  Panel D of Figure
9:297:27574:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:3 shows an increasing number of states have adopted the federal definition of the state tax base for state tax
9:298:27684:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:purposes.  This policy choice limits the extent to which state lawmakers can tinker with the tax base, but also
9:299:27795:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:puts states at risk of changes in federal policy that may have adverse effects on state tax revenues.  The panel
9:300:27907:18:18:63:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:also shows a slight increase in the number of states adopting throwback rules that limit the ability of companies
9:301:28020:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:to have “nowhere income” under state apportionment rules, especially in later years.  Similarly, many states
9:302:28128:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:adopted combined reporting rules that strengthen the reporting requirements for unitary businesses.  This panel
9:303:28239:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:also shows that states have moved away from allowing federal income taxes to be deducted from state taxation.
9:304:28348:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:The most notable change is the reduction in the number of states adopting bonus depreciation in the early
9:305:28453:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:2000s, which is likely due in part to the substantial fiscal cost of these provisions in a period of reduced tax
9:306:28565:18:18:63:162:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenues (Ohrn, 2016).
9:307:28587:18:18:78:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:The  structure  of  the  corporate  tax  system  has  been  an  active  area  for  state  policymakers.   Contrary  to
9:308:28705:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:conventional wisdom, we do not find evidence of a temporal concomitance in tax rate and tax base changes.15
9:309:28812:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:While  some  aspects  of  the  tax  base  have  become  more  generous  for  corporations  (e.g.,  loss  carryforward
9:310:28929:18:18:63:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f6:B:provisions  and  R&D  and  investment  tax  credits),  changes  in  other  rules  have  broadened  the  tax  base  (e.g.
9:311:29049:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:throwback and combined reporting rules).  The following section explores the degree to which these changes to
9:312:29158:18:42:63:329:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:states’ corporate tax systems explain changes in tax revenue.

10:414:33882:7:12:73:534:92:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:18We present further results of this variance decomposition in TableA7.  For example, when we control for an interaction of
10:415:34005:12:0:63:434:80:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:throwback rules and apportionment weights, the explanatory power of the throwback rule increases.
11:416:34103:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:positive and relatively large compared the overall contribution to the variance shown in Panel B. The largest
11:417:34212:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:negative correlate is an indicator for having a franchise tax, which is more common among southern states and
11:418:34321:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:sometimes substitutes for having any corporate tax system at all (e.g., Texas).19Most of the base and credit
11:419:34429:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:provisions listed are positively related to revenue as a share of GDP, except for federal income tax deductiblitly,
11:420:34544:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:loss provisions, and depreciation provisions, which are associated with less corporate tax revenue as a share of
11:421:34656:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:GDP. Overall, tax base and credit rules account for the majority of the explained variation in corporate tax
11:422:34764:18:18:63:185:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenues as a share of GDP.
11:423:34791:18:18:78:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Figure  6  shows  that  the  explanatory  power  of  base  and  credit  rules  has  evolved  over  time.   Specifically,
11:424:34911:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:it shows the share of variation for each five-year interval from 1980-2010 that can be explained by the state
11:425:35020:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax structure in Panel A, rates versus base and credit rules in Panel B, and for each base rule in Panel
11:426:35134:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:C. The upper left panel shows that the state tax policy parameters explain roughly half of the variation in state
11:427:35247:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax revenues as a share of state GDP. The upper right panel shows that a larger share of the explained
11:428:35359:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:variance is accounted for by state corporate tax base rules.  Sales apportionment weights and loss provisions
11:429:35468:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:were quite important in the first half of the sample period.  More recently, however, federal provisions (such as
11:430:35581:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:adopting the federal tax base and federal bonus depreciation or allowing for the deductibility of federal taxes)
11:431:35693:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:have grown in importance.  Additionally, franchise taxes and loss carryforward provisions have also increased
11:432:35802:18:42:63:207:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:their share of explained variance.
11:433:35836:42:28:63:472:395:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:4    Impacts on State Tax Revenue and Economic Activity
11:434:35891:28:18:63:542:367:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We now analyze how taxes impact state tax revenue and economic activity.  Equation1 shows that tax base
11:435:35994:18:18:63:542:349:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:controls should be included when estimating the effects of state taxes on state outcomes.  In this section we
11:436:36103:18:18:63:542:331:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:focus on the extent to which omitting state corporate tax base affects these estimates.  We first explore an event
11:437:36217:18:18:63:542:313:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:study approach that flexibly captures the dynamic effects of tax changes.  We then summarize these results
11:438:36323:18:35:63:282:295:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:with a more parsimonious regression specification.
11:439:36373:35:24:63:229:260:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:4.1    Event Study Estimates
11:440:36401:24:18:63:542:236:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We begin with an analysis of the typical path of state outcomes preceding and following a change in the state
11:441:36510:18:33:63:382:218:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax structure.  We use an event study specification of the form:
11:442:36584:33:0:141:209:185:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:?:Yst=αs+γt+
11:443:36594:0:22:250:264:195:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:∑
