11:455:36970:18:15:63:542:92:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:B:we address imbalance issues by “binning” periods greater than 5 or less than -4, which is reflected in the ̄β
11:456:37079:15:0:73:348:77:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:19See Appendix FigureA6for a map of which states have franchise taxes.
12:457:37151:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:andβcoefficients that are assumed to be stable within end point bins.  To address serial correlation inεit, all
12:458:37262:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:standard errors are clustered by state.  We consider three main outcomes:  state corporate tax revenue as a
12:459:37369:18:18:63:378:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:share of state GDP, log state corporate tax revenue, and log state GDP.
12:460:37440:18:18:78:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:We fit specifications of this type on our state panel data using data from 1980 to 2010.  We also consider
12:461:37546:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:specifications that control for the leads and lags of key components of the tax base.  Specifically, we control
12:462:37657:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for  leads  and  lags  of  the  six  most  important  tax  base  controls  in  terms  of  variance  shares  of  corporate  tax
12:463:37783:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenue:  federal income tax treated as state base, sales apportionment weight, throwback rules, federal income
12:464:37894:18:18:63:299:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax deductibility, loss carryforward, and franchise tax.
12:465:37950:18:18:78:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 7 shows the results for corporate tax cuts and corporate tax increases that exceed a 0.5 percentage
12:466:38056:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:point change in the rate in absolute value on state outcomes.20Panel A shows that corporate tax decreases
12:467:38161:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:that exceed 0.5 percentage point cuts in the rate tend to reduce state corporate tax revenue as a share of state
12:468:38273:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:GDP by roughly 6 percentage points cumulatively over a 5 year period.  Panels B and C show the importance
12:469:38378:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of the numerator and denominator separately.  Despite modestly higher economic activity, corporate tax cuts
12:470:38485:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:decrease state tax revenue by roughly 10%.  The increases in state GDP are imprecise and not statistically
12:471:38591:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:different than zero, though the point estimate is roughly 2%.  Controlling for the tax base does not alter these
12:472:38703:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:general patterns.  Panels D, E, and F show that tax increases have symmetric impacts, though pre-trends are
12:473:38810:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:a bit more noticeable prior to state corporate tax increases.  Specifically, the event studies in D and E show
12:474:38920:18:18:63:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:that tax revenues were also higher preceding the tax increase events by roughly a similar magnitude, so it is
12:475:39029:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:not clear that corporate tax revenues actually increase following tax increases.  We view these event studies as
12:476:39141:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:describing the typical evolution of outcomes before and after tax changes.  Since these tax changes potentially
12:477:39252:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:include some endogenous changes that are intended to address current (or expected) economic conditions, these
12:478:39361:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:impacts are descriptive and not causal.21Overall,  these point estimates of the effect of state corporate tax
12:479:39470:18:18:63:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes are imprecise, but the key finding for our purposes is that they do not depend strongly on base controls
12:480:39582:18:35:63:112:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:on average.
12:481:39593:35:24:63:219:276:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:4.2    Regression Estimates
12:482:39620:24:33:63:486:252:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We summarize these relationships by estimating equation2 with state and year fixed effects, i.e.,
12:483:39717:33:18:213:392:219:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:?:Rst=αs+φt+γτst+X′stΨBASEst+ust,
12:484:39748:18:12:73:516:201:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:20We focus on the impacts of non-trivial changes in state corporate tax rates and present analogous results for all state
12:485:39869:12:10:63:533:189:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:changes in Appendix FigureA23.  The threshold of 0.5 percentage points includes roughly half the state corporate tax changes
12:486:39993:10:9:63:531:179:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:(see Appendix FigureA24for a histogram).  A corporate tax cut that exceeds 0.5 percentage points amounts to roughly a one
12:487:40114:9:10:63:529:170:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:percentage point cut in state corporate tax rate on average.  On average, a corporate tax increase that exceeds 0.5 percentage
12:488:40240:10:9:63:537:160:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:points corresponds to a 1.5 percentage point increase in the state corporate tax rate.  Controlling for leads and lags of the other
12:489:40371:9:10:63:535:151:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:tax base controls (in addition to the ones in our baseline specification) results in similar but slightly noisier estimates as shown
12:490:40503:10:9:63:80:141:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:in Appendix FigureA26.21
12:491:40527:9:10:81:523:132:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:For example, macroeconomic shocks might induce changes in state corporate tax systems.  Appendix FigureA25shows
12:492:40638:10:0:63:533:122:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:analogous results to Figure7 for the subset of state corporate tax changes thatGiroud and Rauh(2015) classify as exogenous.
13:493:40763:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This specification increases statistical precision relative to the event study equation4 by combining the periods
13:494:40876:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:before and after tax changes and by imposing symmetry in the effects of tax increases and decreases.22Column
13:495:40984:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:(1) of Table5 shows results when we omit tax base controls.  This estimate implies that increasing the state
13:496:41092:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax rate by 1 percentage point leads to an increase in corporate tax revenues relative to GDP of
13:497:41198:18:18:63:541:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:B:1.8 basis points.  Relative to the average value ofRstof 35 basis points,  a 1 percentage point increase inτ
13:498:41306:18:18:63:249:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:represents a (1.8/35=) 5% increase inRst.
13:499:41347:18:18:78:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Column (2) of Table5 shows that including controls for the tax base does not affect this estimate, which
13:500:41451:18:18:63:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:reinforces  the  results  from  the  event  studies  in  Figure7.   However,  including  these  controls  increases  the
13:501:41571:18:18:63:543:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:precision of the estimate.  As we discussed in Section3,  these controls have large explanatory power on the
13:502:41679:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenue-to-GDP ratio.  The coefficients on the tax base controls have a similar interpretation as those in Figure
13:503:41792:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:5.   For  instance,  some  controls  that  narrow  the  base  —  including  the  R&D  tax  credit,  the  investment  tax
13:504:41912:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:credit, and an indicator for allowing the deductibility of federal income taxes — have negative effects onRst.
13:505:42022:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Conversely,  controls that correspond to broader bases,  such as throwback rules or incremental tax bases for
13:506:42131:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:R&D tax credits, have positive effects onRst.  Having a franchise tax also negatively impactsRst, as states
13:507:42238:18:32:63:411:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:with a franchise tax often use it as an alternative to a tax on corporate income.
13:508:42319:32:25:63:154:441:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:C:4.2.1    Base Index
13:509:42338:25:18:63:542:416:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We  can  use  these  estimates  to  construct  a  composite  measure  of  the  tax  base.   We  define  an  index  of  the
13:510:42460:18:0:63:237:398:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:breadth of the tax base:  Base Indexst=
13:511:42499:0:7:241:249:410:7:g_d0_f21:7:g_d0_f21:?:∑
13:512:42500:7:8:250:288:403:5:g_d0_f18:5:g_d0_f18:?:j∈J ̃xjst ̃Ψjst
13:513:42515:8:14:260:542:395:7:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f4:A:σB,whereJis the set of all 15 base and credit controls, and
13:514:42574:14:18:63:542:381:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:where we normalize this index to have unit standard deviation.  A regression that replaces the base controls
13:515:42682:18:18:63:543:363:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:with the Base Index recoversσBas a regression coefficient.  We report this estimate in the bottom of Column
13:516:42789:18:18:63:542:345:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:(2),  which is statistically significant at the 1-percent level,  and implies that increasing the Base Index by 1
13:517:42902:18:32:63:345:327:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:standard deviation leads to an increase inRstof 30 basis points.
13:518:42966:32:25:63:303:295:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:C:4.2.2    Separating Effects on Revenue and GDP
13:519:43012:25:17:63:542:270:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Taxes  may  affect  the  revenue-to-GDP  ratio  by  increasing  revenues  or  by  decreasing  GDP.  We  estimate  the
13:520:43129:17:18:63:542:253:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:effects on the numerator and denominator separately. To facilitate comparisons across states and across time, we
13:521:43241:18:18:63:542:235:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:present estimates of the effects on log state corporate tax revenue and on log state GDP. For these specifications
13:522:43355:18:18:63:542:217:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:we report the effect of the log keep rate,i.e., ln(1−τ).23Columns (3) and (5) of Table5 show that an increase
13:523:43464:18:18:63:542:199:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in the log keep rate reduces revenue and increases GDP. Columns (4) and (6) further show that controlling
13:524:43569:18:18:63:542:181:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for the tax base does not have large effects on these estimates.  However, some tax base controls affect these
13:525:43679:18:18:63:542:163:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:outcomes even when the effect onRstis not statistically significant.  For instance, states with a franchise tax
13:526:43790:18:15:63:542:145:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:and states that allow for the deductibility of federal income taxes have both lower revenues and lower GDP.24
13:527:43899:15:12:73:535:130:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:22In these estimations we weight observations by the mean GDP in the state over our sample, and the standard errors allow
13:528:44020:12:10:63:537:118:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:for arbitrary correlation between observations from a given state.  We scale the revenue-to-GDP variable so that coefficients can
13:529:44149:10:9:63:80:108:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:be interpreted in terms of basis points.23
13:530:44191:9:9:81:525:99:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:We use ln(1−τ) because these expressions are in log form and the keep rate formulation avoids taking logs of zeros for
13:531:44309:9:7:63:210:90:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:states that have no state corporate tax.
13:532:44349:7:12:73:527:83:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:24It may also be the case that tax base controls have dynamic effects on these outcomes.  A full discussion of the effects of
13:533:44474:12:0:63:525:71:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:each base control is beyond the scope of this paper.  Nonetheless, Appendix FiguresA30-A44present results of event studies
14:534:44598:0:28:63:397:724:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:5    Heterogeneous Effects of Tax Rate Changes
14:535:44644:28:18:63:542:696:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This section relaxes the assumption of homogeneous treatment effects ofτ.  We show that tax base interactions
14:536:44753:18:18:63:542:678:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:with the tax rate can lead to heterogeneous effects across time and states, and that omitting these interactions
14:537:44865:18:18:63:466:660:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:leads to biased estimates of the average treatment effect of state corporate tax rate changes.
14:538:44959:18:18:78:542:642:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Changes  in  state  corporate  tax  rates  may  have  differential  effects  on  tax  revenue  and  economic  activity
14:539:45077:18:18:63:542:624:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:depending on the breadth of the tax base.  Intuitively, a tax increase should raise less revenue whenever the
14:540:45186:18:18:63:542:606:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax base is relatively narrow.  This intuition holds (1) for mechanical effects, since narrow bases by definition
14:541:45299:18:18:63:542:588:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax a smaller share of profits; (2) for reporting responses, since firms in states with narrow bases may respond
14:542:45411:18:18:63:542:570:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:by adopting new deduction strategies; and (3) for behavioral responses, since firms are likely to respond less to
14:543:45524:18:17:63:542:552:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:a tax increase whenever the tax affects a smaller share of their profits.25As a hypothetical example, suppose
14:544:45633:17:18:63:542:535:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:that California and New York both increase their state corporate tax rates, but suppose further that California
14:545:45744:18:18:63:542:517:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:has a much more lenient treatment of loss carryforward provisions.  Firms in California with past losses will
14:546:45853:18:18:63:542:499:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:face a smaller increase in their effective tax liability as firms in New York, since the tax base in California is
14:547:45967:18:18:63:542:481:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:narrower.  Any behavioral response by firms that depends on current rates, such as investment, employment,
14:548:46073:18:18:63:542:463:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:or relocation, will therefore be more muted in California than in New York.  While this example only mentions
14:549:46182:18:18:63:542:445:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:loss carryforward provisions, the treatment of other aspects of the tax base, such as depreciation allowances or
14:550:46294:18:35:63:475:427:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:investment tax credits, may also modulate the degree to which tax changes affect tax revenue.
14:551:46387:35:24:63:223:392:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:5.1    Econometric Intuition
14:552:46415:24:18:63:542:368:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:When the effect of a state corporate tax rate change depends on the tax base, estimates that do not account for
14:553:46526:18:18:63:542:350:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax-base-driven heterogeneity can lead to bias in average treatment effects.  The intuition for this bias follows
14:554:46639:18:18:63:542:332:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:directly from the Omitted Variable Bias (OVB) formula.  For simplicity, consider the case in which there are
14:555:46747:18:18:63:542:314:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:two types of states with narrow and broad bases, and that the effects of tax changes depend on the tax base.
14:556:46855:18:33:63:161:296:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:The long regression is:
14:557:46878:33:33:146:459:263:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:?:Rst=α+β1τst+β2τst×I{Narrow Base}st+δI{Narrow Base}st+ust.
14:558:46935:33:18:63:542:230:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:If we assume that the effect of a tax rate change in broad-base states (β1) is greater than in narrow-base states
14:559:47048:18:18:63:542:212:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:(β1+β2), we might worry that a short regression that omits the interaction termτst×I{Narrow Base}stwill
14:560:47151:18:18:63:542:194:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:yield a biased estimate of the average effect across states,  i.e.,β1+β2Pr(Narrow Base).  The OVB formula
14:561:47256:18:32:63:312:176:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:shows that the short regression estimate will be biased:26
14:562:47314:32:7:75:297:144:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f4:A:E[b1] =β1+β2×Cov(τst,τst×I{Narrow Base}st)
14:563:47356:7:0:207:244:137:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f4:?:Var(τst)
14:564:47364:0:7:300:527:144:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:=β1+β2Pr(Narrow Base)×Var(τst|Narrow Base)
14:565:47406:7:0:460:497:137:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f4:?:Var(τst)
14:566:47414:0:25:528:531:144:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:?:.
14:567:47415:25:10:63:530:119:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:around changes in the tax base controls.  From these graphs, the most interesting case is the adoption of incremental tax base
14:568:47541:10:7:63:451:109:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:for R&D tax credits, which led to tax increases in future years by limiting the value of R&D tax credits.
14:569:47646:7:13:73:540:102:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:F:25Indeed, our derivation above implies that the marginal effect of taxes will depend on the base through both mechanical and
14:570:47770:13:7:63:274:89:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:behavioral effects of taxes:dRdτ=B(τ,X) +τ×dB(τ,X)dτ.
14:571:47823:7:0:73:391:82:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f22:A:26Where the short regression is given by:Rst=a+b1τst+dI{Narrow Base}st+ust.
15:572:47900:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:The sign and magnitude of the bias is governed by two forces:  (1) heterogeneous effects due to the tax base
15:573:48008:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:interactions  (i.e.,β2≷0)  and  (2)  the  covariance  between  the  interaction  term  andτ.   First,  the  sign  and
15:574:48125:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:magnitude of the effect of tax base provisionβ2depends on the base rule.  For base-narrowing provisions, we
15:575:48232:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:expectβ2<0.  Second, the termβ2is scaled by the covariance between the tax rate and the interaction.  In
15:576:48336:18:18:63:543:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:contrast to the average treatment effect, which scalesβ2by the fraction of the population with a narrow base,
15:577:48445:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the short regression scalesβ2by a different term.27In the case of indicator variables, this scaling term is the
15:578:48556:18:18:63:384:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:conditional variance of the state corporate tax rate in narrow-base states.
15:579:48631:18:18:78:543:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Ifβ2<0  and  narrow-base  states  change  taxes  more  frequently  (i.e.,Var(τst|Narrow Base)>Var(τst)),
15:580:48735:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:then omitting the interaction term will result in a downwardly-biased estimate of the average effect of taxes
15:581:48844:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:on revenues.  The general case with 15 interactions is slightly more complex, but the potential biases from not
15:582:48955:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:including interactions have a similar intuition.  This type of bias is well known in the econometrics literature
15:583:49067:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:(e.g.,Wooldridge(2005)),  and  has  been  shown  to  be  empirically  important  across  several  fields  of  applied
15:584:49184:17:35:63:315:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:economics (Gibbons, Su ́arez Serrato and Urbancic,2014).
15:585:49240:35:25:63:429:474:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:5.2    Estimates of Heterogeneous Effects of Tax Rate Changes
15:586:49301:25:18:63:542:449:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:To  explore  tax-base-driven  heterogeneity,  we  expand  the  model  of  equation2  to  include  interaction  terms
15:587:49417:18:34:63:270:431:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:between the tax rate and the tax base controls:
15:588:49464:34:0:175:279:397:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:?:Rst=αs+γt+β0τst+
15:589:49480:0:24:284:295:410:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f17:?:15∑
15:590:49483:24:0:281:295:386:7:g_d0_f11:7:g_d0_f5:?:j=1
15:591:49486:0:38:297:542:397:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:A:βjτst× ̃xjst+ ̃x′st ̃ΨBASEst+ust,(5)
15:592:49522:38:18:63:542:359:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:where   ̃xj’s  are  the  standardized  base  rules,  which  facilitates  the  interpretation  ofβ0as  the  mean  effect  of
15:593:49645:18:18:63:542:341:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:B:τ.   Column  (1)  of  Table6  presents  the  results  from  a  model  that  controls  for  the  tax  base  but  that  omits
15:594:49768:18:18:63:542:323:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:interactions  (as  in  Column  (2)  of  Table5),  and  Column  (2)  includes  the  interactions.   In  contrast  to  the
15:595:49888:18:18:63:542:305:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:results of Table5,  we find that including interaction terms leads to a larger average effect of the corporate
15:596:49998:18:17:63:542:287:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax rate on the revenue-to-GDP ratio, with the estimate increasing from 1.6 to 2.4 basis points.  This effect
15:597:50107:17:18:63:542:270:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:is 50% larger, which is strong evidence that tax-base interactions matter and that the OLS estimator is not a
15:598:50216:18:18:63:543:252:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:consistent estimator for the average effect across states.  Relative to the mean value ofRst= 35 basis points,
15:599:50326:18:18:63:490:234:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:a 1 percentage point increase inτleads to a (2.4/35 =) 7% increase in the revenue-to-GDP ratio.
15:600:50421:18:36:78:413:216:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:For a given state with a tax base ̃xst, the total effect ofτonRstis given by:
15:601:50498:36:0:229:308:180:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f11:?:βR( ̃xst) =β0+σJ
15:602:50514:0:24:324:335:192:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f17:?:15∑
15:603:50517:24:0:321:335:168:7:g_d0_f11:7:g_d0_f5:?:k=1
15:604:50520:0:14:339:348:187:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f11:?:βk
15:605:50522:14:0:338:348:173:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f11:?:σJ
15:606:50524:0:17:351:363:180:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f11:?: ̃xkst
15:607:50530:17:10:321:363:163:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:︸︷︷︸
15:608:50534:10:0:311:373:153:7:g_d0_f5:7:g_d0_f5:?:Joint Interactions
15:609:50552:0:55:373:542:180:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:A:,(6)
15:610:50556:55:0:63:350:125:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:whereσJequals the standard deviation of the linear combination
15:611:50618:0:14:357:381:136:10:g_d0_f17:7:g_d0_f5:?:(∑15
15:612:50622:14:0:373:407:122:7:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f10:?:k=1βk ̃x
15:613:50630:0:7:406:410:129:7:g_d0_f11:7:g_d0_f11:?:k
15:614:50631:7:0:406:413:122:7:g_d0_f11:7:g_d0_f11:?:st
15:615:50633:0:11:414:420:136:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:?:)
15:616:50634:11:18:419:542:125:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:.  The joint interaction term
15:617:50663:18:15:63:542:107:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:has mean zero,  since the   ̃xkst’s are normalized,  and a unit standard deviation since we divide byσJ.28The
15:618:50772:15:13:73:537:92:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:27Except in knife-edge cases, these weights do not coincide with sample frequencies and the resulting weighted average is not
15:619:50897:13:9:63:80:79:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:representative of the average effect across states.28
15:620:50950:9:0:81:529:70:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:We first estimate5 to recoverβk’s.  By construction, the estimate ofβ0is not affected by this procedure.  Note also that,
16:621:51073:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:specification in equation6 has two main advantages.  First, the joint interaction term is a useful data-reduction
16:622:51186:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:measure that captures the variation across 15 bases in a single index.  Second, the statistical significance of the
16:623:51301:18:18:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the total effectβR(Xst) for a given state depends on the covariance matrix of the individualβkterms.  While
16:624:51408:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:it is hard to evaluate the joint statistical importance of these interactions from individual coefficients, the joint
16:625:51525:18:18:63:519:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:interaction term collapses the covariance structure and allows for a simple univariate statistical analysis.
16:626:51633:18:18:78:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Column  (2)  in  Table6  reports  the  coefficient  on  the  joint  interactions.   The  joint  interaction  term  is
16:627:51750:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:statistically  significant  and  shows  that  interactions  between  the  tax  rate  and  the  tax  base  are  economically
16:628:51873:18:18:63:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:important.  For instance, a 1 percentage point tax increase in a state with a joint interaction term that is two
16:629:51985:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:standard deviations above the mean would increaseRstby (2.4 + 2×1.25≈) 5 basis points.  Conversely,  a
16:630:52087:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:state with a joint interaction term that is two standard deviations below the mean would not see an increase
16:631:52195:18:18:63:118:544:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:in revenue.29
16:632:52208:18:17:78:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Columns (3)-(6) in Table6 report the effects of ln(1−τ) on log-GDP and log-revenue.  As before, controlling
16:633:52315:17:18:63:543:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for the tax base does not have large effects on our estimates ofβ0.  While an increase in ln(1−τ) both reduces
16:634:52425:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenue  and  increases  GDP,  we  find  that  the  effects  on  revenue  are  a  larger  driver  of  the  net  effect  on  the
16:635:52552:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenue-to-GDP ratio.  In addition, these columns also show that both state GDP and state tax revenue are
16:636:52657:18:18:63:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:subject to statistically significant joint interactions between ln(1−τ) and the tax base.  For the case of log-
16:637:52768:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenue, we find that the mean effect is much larger in Column (4) than in Column (3), while the mean effect
16:638:52876:18:18:63:317:419:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:B:β0on log-GDP is less affected by introducing interactions.
16:639:52934:18:18:78:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:This joint interaction term can be decomposed into the individual interactions, which are presented in the
16:640:53040:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:remaining rows of Table6.30Figure8 further describes how each of the interaction terms contributes to the
16:641:53145:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:joint interaction term for each outcome.  Panel A plots the fraction of the variation in the total effectβY( ̃xst)
16:642:53259:18:18:63:542:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for  each  outcome  that  is  driven  by  each  of  the  base  controls.   Each  contribution  in  this  graph  is  driven  by
16:643:53385:18:18:63:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the coefficient of each interaction term, as well as by the number of tax base changes for each control.  This
16:644:53495:18:18:63:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:figure shows that the heterogeneous effects for the revenue-to-GDP ratio are driven mostly by the R&D tax
16:645:53600:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:credit, the presence of a franchise tax, the allowance for federal accelerated depreciation, and the deduction of
16:646:53713:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:federal taxes.  Of these four policies, the franchise tax and the allowance for federal depreciation drive variation
16:647:53829:18:17:63:542:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:through heterogeneous effects on corporate revenue, while the allowance for the deductibility of federal taxes
16:648:53939:17:18:63:542:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:has a larger effect on GDP. For example, a 1 percentage point tax increase in a state with a franchise tax would
16:649:54051:18:18:63:542:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:increaseRstby (2.4 + 0.7×1≈) 3.1 basis points, while an equal increase in a state without a franchise tax
16:650:54156:18:18:63:543:204:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:would only increaseRstby (2.4 + 0.7×0 =) 2.4 basis points.  Panel B splits this decomposition by five-year
16:651:54262:18:18:63:542:186:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:intervals, and shows that the importance of the franchise tax and the deductibility of federal taxes has waned
16:652:54372:18:18:63:542:168:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:over time, while the importance of the allowance for federal accelerated depreciation and the R&D tax credit
16:653:54480:18:18:63:218:150:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:has grown in importance over time.
16:654:54514:18:9:63:80:132:8:g_d0_f8:6:g_d0_f7:F:without the standardization of the joint interaction term, we would obtain a coefficient of one on this variable.29
16:655:54629:9:10:81:534:123:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:A:These results are robust to including lagged values of the the tax rate, the tax base, and the joint interactions.  TableA10
16:656:54753:10:9:63:535:113:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:shows that controlling for 1-5 lags of any of these variables does not affect the total cumulative mean effect of tax rates on rev-
16:657:54884:9:7:63:246:104:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:enues.  See the note to TableA10for more detail.
16:658:54932:7:12:73:523:97:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:30We expect interaction terms to have a positive coefficient whenever they rules broaden the base.  Conversely, we expect
16:659:55053:12:0:63:509:85:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:negative coefficients for rules that narrow the base.  In AppendixA.2, we list these predictions for each interaction term.
17:660:55178:0:25:63:544:724:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:F:5.3    Tax Base Trends and Implications for the Revenue Responses to Rate Changes
17:661:55259:25:18:63:542:699:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We now evaluate howβY( ̃xst) varies across states and over time due to changes in the state corporate tax base
17:662:55369:18:18:63:542:681:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f4:B: ̃xst.  Figure 9 plots the average value ofβY( ̃xst) in a given yeart, and shows that changes in tax bases between
17:663:55483:18:17:63:542:663:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:1980 and 2000 diminished the effect of taxes on revenue.  Consistent with the descriptive evidence in favor of
17:664:55593:17:18:63:543:646:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:narrowing tax bases in Section2, this figure shows that tax cuts lead to smaller reductions in 2000 than 1980.
17:665:55703:18:18:63:542:628:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This  figure  also  shows  that  this  pattern is  slightly reversed  during  the  2000’s.   Two  trends that  we  observe
17:666:55825:18:18:63:542:610:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:during this time are the adoption of combined reporting, which tightens the reporting requirements for unitary
17:667:55935:18:18:63:542:592:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:businesses, and of throwback rules, which limit the extent to which firms can have “nowhere income” under
17:668:56040:18:18:63:180:574:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the apportionment system.
17:669:56065:18:18:78:542:556:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Figure9  shows  how  the  state  average  has  evolved,  but  masks  considerable  heterogeneity  across  states.
17:670:56178:18:18:63:542:538:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Figure10plots the estimated total effectβY( ̃xst) for four selected states during our sample period.  Delaware,
17:671:56289:18:18:63:542:520:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for example, narrowed its tax base, which is reflected by a decrease in the effect of a tax change on revenue
17:672:56398:18:18:63:542:502:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:over time.  This pattern is due to changes to the Delaware corporate tax base in the late 1990’s that led to
17:673:56506:18:18:63:542:484:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:an  increase  in  the  number  of  years  allowed  for  loss  carryforward,  and  by  the  adoption  of  a  generous  R&D
17:674:56627:18:18:63:542:466:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax credit.  In contrast,  Michigan broadened its tax base by disallowing both the MACRS depreciation rule
17:675:56733:18:18:63:542:448:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and federal accelerated and bonus depreciation rules.  In addition, the adoption of throwback and combined
17:676:56839:18:18:63:542:430:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:reporting  rules  in  the  late  2000’s  further  broadened  the  tax  base.   As  a  result,  the  second  panel  in  Figure
17:677:56964:18:18:63:542:412:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:10shows  that  revenue  became  more  responsive  to  changes  in  tax  rates  in  the  later  years  of  our  sample  for
17:678:57086:18:17:63:542:394:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Michigan.  Pennsylvania and Rhode Island are examples of states whose experience mirrors the reversal pattern
17:679:57195:17:18:63:542:377:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:observed on average across states.  Pennsylvania narrowed its tax base in the 1990’s by increasing the number
17:680:57304:18:18:63:542:359:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of years allowed for loss carryforward, as well as introducing R&D and investment tax credits.  In the 2000’s, it
17:681:57417:18:18:63:542:341:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:reversed this trend by reducing the investment tax credit and introducing throwback and combined reporting
17:682:57523:18:18:63:542:323:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:rules.  In Rhode Island,  the narrowing of the base was due to the introduction of R&D and investment tax
17:683:57628:18:42:63:432:305:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:credits, and the reversal was due to the disallowance of federal bonus depreciation.31
17:684:57714:42:28:63:306:263:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:6    Revenue-Maximizing-Tax Rate
17:685:57746:28:18:63:542:235:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This section evaluates how the structure of the state corporate tax system determines the revenue-maximizing-
17:686:57855:18:18:63:100:217:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax rate.
17:687:57864:18:15:78:542:199:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:We extend the framework in equation1 by introducing a quadratic term that can capture the degree to
17:688:57963:15:12:73:540:184:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:F:31Appendix FigureA47shows the total effect for each state year, which can be compared to the base changes by state in Ap-
17:689:58084:12:9:63:539:172:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:pendix FiguresA7-A19.  Appendix FigureA48compares the estimated effect across all states in 1985 and 2005.  These maps are
17:690:58206:9:10:63:535:163:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:consistent with the trends in Figure9, as the map in 2005 has more states with effects closer to zero.  However, this average ef-
17:691:58335:10:9:63:533:153:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:fect masks considerable heterogeneity in experiences across states.  In addition to Michigan, other mid-western states including
17:692:58463:9:10:63:535:144:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:Wisconsin, Ohio, and Illinois saw a broadening of the tax base between 1985 and 2000.  In contrast, several other states includ-
17:693:58591:10:9:63:529:134:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:ing California, Oregon, Florida, and Massachusetts saw a narrowing of the tax base, as evidenced by the diminished effects of
17:694:58716:9:0:63:180:125:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:taxes on corporate tax revenue.
18:695:58749:0:33:63:456:724:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:which tax rate increases raise progressively less revenue, or even result in revenue losses:32
18:696:58843:33:33:219:542:691:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:A:Rst=β0τst+δ0(τst)2+αs+γt+ust.(7)

18:704:59119:27:18:78:542:577:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Panel A of Table 7 presents estimates of this regression.  Columns (1) and (2) present specifications with
18:705:59225:18:18:63:542:559:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and without state fixed effects.  These columns show positive estimates forβ0, but the inclusion of state fixed

18:707:59447:18:17:63:542:523:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:regressions do not detect decreasing returns of increasing taxes, which may be due to the relatively low tax
18:708:59555:17:18:63:542:506:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:rates  observed  in  the  data.   Since  the  implied  relationship  between  tax  rates  and  corporate  tax  revenues  is
18:709:59678:18:18:63:469:488:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:convex, we cannot identify a revenue-maximizing-tax rate using these estimates ofβ0andδ0.
18:710:59767:18:18:78:542:470:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:As in the previous section,  we are interested in the possibility that the responsiveness to taxes,  and the
18:711:59875:18:18:63:542:452:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:implied revenue-maximizing-tax rate, depend on the breadth of the tax base.  We explore this possibility by
18:712:59982:18:18:63:542:434:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:allowing the linear and quadratic effects of taxes to depend on the Base Indexstdefined in Section 4.2.1.  This
18:713:60093:18:18:63:542:416:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:measure is mean-zero by construction.  A higher value of the Base Indexstmeans that the tax base is broader
18:714:60200:18:18:63:456:398:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in the sense that the tax base controls are associated with a higher revenue-to-GDP ratio.
18:715:60290:18:33:78:312:380:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Armed with this measure, we estimate the regression:

18:726:61034:18:18:63:542:156:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the  revenue-maximizing  rate  at  the  mean  value  of  the  base  index  yields  a  value  ofτ∗(Base Indexst=  0)  of
18:727:61153:18:18:63:542:138:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:27%.  Panel A of Figure11plots the estimated relation between the state corporate tax rate andRstat the
18:728:61256:18:15:63:542:120:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:value Base Indexst= 0.  We also explore the heterogeneity inτ∗(Base Indexst) that is implied by variation in
18:729:61364:15:13:73:530:105:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:32Clausing (2007), Devereux(2007), andKawano and Slemrod(2015) discuss results of similar specifications using data on
18:730:61482:13:9:63:126:92:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:OECD countries.
18:731:61497:9:0:73:411:83:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f27:A:33The marginal effect ofτon revenue isdRstdτ=β0+ 2δ0×τ.  For small taxes we havedRstdτ
18:732:61583:0:10:417:420:90:8:g_d0_f26:8:g_d0_f26:?:∣∣
18:733:61585:10:0:417:472:80:8:g_d0_f26:8:g_d0_f8:?:∣τ=0=β0>0.
19:734:61597:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Base Indexst.  Panel B of Figure11plots the cumulative distribution function of the estimatedτ∗(Base Indexst)
19:735:61706:18:18:63:542:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for every state-year in our data.  The average revenue-maximizing rate is greater than 45% and the minimum
19:736:61812:18:18:63:366:688:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:value is greater than any corporate tax rate we observe in the data.34
19:737:61882:18:18:78:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Changes in corporate tax rates affect local economic activity and other forms of tax revenue.  Indeed, in
19:738:61987:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Su ́arez Serrato and Zidar(2016) we show that changes to state corporate tax rates affect the location decisions
19:739:62099:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of firms and workers.  These decisions affect the demand and supply of labor, which influences local population
19:740:62210:18:18:63:542:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and income.  As a result, state tax revenue from personal income taxes and sales taxes may also be affected
19:741:62317:18:18:63:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:by changes in state corporate tax rates.  We quantify the importance of these fiscal externalities by estimating
19:742:62429:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:equations7  and8  on  total  tax  revenue  as  a  share  of  state  GDP.  Panel  B  of  Table7  presents  estimates  for
19:743:62549:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:these regressions.  These results are qualitatively similar to those in Panel A, in that we do not find statistically
19:744:62666:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:significant decreasing returns to taxation on total tax revenue.  Panel C of Figure11plots the estimated relation
19:745:62779:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:between the corporate tax rate and the total tax revenue-to-GDP ratio at the mean value of Base Indexst= 0,
19:746:62886:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:and shows that a tax rate of 9.6% maximizes total state tax revenue.  Panel D of Figure11plots the CDF
19:747:62988:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of the estimated revenue-maximizing-tax rates and shows a much more compressed distribution that centers
19:748:63092:18:18:63:542:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:around 10%.  As shown in Figure1, only a few states have ever had tax rates above 10%, and this fraction has
19:749:63200:18:18:63:180:455:10:g_d0_f4:7:g_d0_f5:B:been declining over time.35
19:750:63227:18:18:78:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Given the lack of precision in these estimates, we interpret these results as suggesting that the data do not
19:751:63336:18:18:63:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:show strong patterns of decreasing returns from increasing taxes.  At the current levels of corporate tax rates,
19:752:63448:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:we can rule out the hypothesis that, for states with corporate tax rates below 10%, cutting corporate tax rates
19:753:63559:18:42:63:247:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:has tended to raise corporate tax revenue.
19:754:63601:42:28:63:320:341:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:7    Discussion of Policy Implications
19:755:63639:28:18:63:542:313:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:This paper has established several facts detailing how state tax rates,  base rules,  and credits determine the
19:756:63750:18:18:63:542:295:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:structure  of  the  state  corporate  tax  system.   We  find  that  changes  to  tax  base  rules  and  credits  are  more
19:757:63873:18:18:63:542:277:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:common than changes in tax rates,  and that changes in tax base rules are not enacted to temporally offset
19:758:63979:18:17:63:542:259:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:changes to tax rates.  Further, we show that changes in tax base rules and credits play a more important role
19:759:64088:17:18:63:542:242:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in explaining patterns in the revenue-to-GDP ratio across states than do changes in tax rates.  We document
19:760:64195:18:18:63:542:224:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:trends in individual tax base rules over time and provide evidence that, while some states have broadened their
19:761:64306:18:18:63:542:206:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:tax bases by adopting combined reporting and throwback rules in recent years, most other measures of the tax
19:762:64414:18:18:63:542:188:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:base point toward a narrowing of the tax base.  We analyze the role that tax base rules play in the estimation
19:763:64524:18:18:63:542:170:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of the effects of tax rates on tax revenues and economic activity, and find that controlling for these rules does
19:764:64637:18:18:63:542:152:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:not affect the estimated effects.  Instead, we show that accounting for heterogeneous effects of tax changes that
19:765:64750:18:15:63:542:134:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:depend on the structure of the corporate tax system is important both to obtain consistent estimates of the
19:766:64857:15:12:73:533:119:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:34For many observations we do not find any evidence of decreasing returns,i.e.,δ1+δ2×Base Indexst>0, which results
19:767:64971:12:10:63:533:107:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:in a value ofτ∗(Base Indexst) of 100%.  This result should not be interpreted as literally suggesting that revenue will be maxi-
19:768:65099:10:9:63:541:97:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:mized with a tax rate of 100%.  Rather, this result suggests that the low values ofτin the data fail to identify a value ofδ0that
19:769:65228:9:7:63:259:88:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:implies strong decreasing returns to increasing taxes.
19:770:65282:7:12:73:527:81:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:35These results are robust to controlling for state personal income taxes and sales taxes, as shown in Appendix TableA12
19:771:65402:12:0:63:162:69:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:and Appendix FigureA49.
20:772:65427:0:18:63:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:average effect of changing taxes, and to more precisely forecast the revenue response of individual states with
20:773:65538:18:18:63:201:706:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:different corporate tax systems.
20:774:65570:18:18:78:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:These findings have important implications for policy.  First, while changes in tax rates receive public and
20:775:65678:18:18:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:media  attention,  changes  in  state  tax  bases  may  have  larger  effects  on  revenue  and  may  also  modulate  the
20:776:65799:18:18:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:effects of state corporate tax rates on revenue and economic activity.  For this reason, the public debate should
20:777:65912:18:18:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:place relatively more attention to policy changes that affect the structure of state corporate taxation, and not
20:778:66024:18:18:63:183:616:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:only the statutory tax rate.
20:779:66052:18:18:78:542:598:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Second, given the large effects of the structure of the tax base on corporate tax revenue, state policymakers
20:780:66161:18:18:63:542:580:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:should be careful to use these policies to accomplish particular goals.  States that are able to attract businesses
20:781:66276:18:18:63:542:562:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for  non-tax  reasons  may  prefer  to  have  a  lower  tax  rate  and  a  broader  base  by,  for  instance,  adopting  the
20:782:66400:18:18:63:542:544:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:federal income tax base as their own.  States wishing to increase investment may depart from this strategy by
20:783:66509:18:17:63:542:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:using tax credits or generous depreciation allowances to encourage investment, but they may see substantial
20:784:66616:17:18:63:542:509:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:declines in revenue.  Finally, states wishing to attract or retain innovative businesses may craft a treatment of
20:785:66729:18:18:63:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:loss carryforward provisions that is very favorable to new businesses.  Policymakers would likely benefit from
20:786:66839:18:18:63:344:473:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:further research outlining the relative success of these strategies.
20:787:66907:18:18:78:542:455:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Third, as states structure the taxation of corporate income for their particular needs and objectives, state
20:788:67015:18:18:63:542:437:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:policymakers should bear in mind that changes to the structure of state corporate taxation will influence the
20:789:67124:18:18:63:542:419:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:distortionary costs of increasing the state corporate tax rate.  In particular, we find that when states narrow
20:790:67235:18:18:63:542:401:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:the tax base, they also diminish the relation between tax rates and corporate tax revenue.  By making it harder
20:791:67346:18:18:63:542:383:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:to raise tax revenue from corporations, it is also likely that state policymakers will be forced to raise revenue
20:792:67459:18:18:63:542:365:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:from other sources including sales taxes, property taxes, or personal income taxes, or to reduce spending on
20:793:67567:18:18:63:121:347:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:public goods.
20:794:67580:18:18:78:542:329:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Future work can explore the degree to which tax base determinants affect the incidence of the state corporate
20:795:67689:18:18:63:542:311:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:income tax by extending the framework in Su ́arez Serrato and Zidar(2016) to allow for deductions that may
20:796:67795:18:18:63:542:293:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:affect the response of firms to tax rate changes.  Intuitively, a narrower tax base lowers the benefits of a tax
20:797:67907:18:18:63:542:275:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:cut to business owners as they only pay taxes on a smaller fraction of profits.  As there is a smaller benefit
20:798:68017:18:17:63:542:257:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:from the tax cut, firms are less likely to enter a particular location, which will also mute the effect of the tax
20:799:68131:17:18:63:542:240:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:cut on employment, wages, and costs of living.  Whether the decrease in firm entry is larger than the decrease
20:800:68241:18:18:63:542:222:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in the real wage and employment will determine the extent to which the incidence of a state income tax cut is
20:801:68350:18:18:63:542:204:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:borne by workers, landowners, or firm owners.  Overall, many exciting questions on the incidence and efficiency
20:802:68461:18:0:63:386:186:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:consequences of reforms to the state corporate tax structure remain open.

35:1098:90857:12:12:63:542:486:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:rate.  A change that represents a narrowing of the base is counted in the−1 column, while a year that represents a broadening of
35:1099:90985:12:12:63:542:474:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:the base is counted as +1.  An increase in the rate of investment credits, R&D credits, or sales apportionment weight corresponds
35:1100:91114:12:12:63:542:462:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:to a narrowing of the base, while a decrease corresponds to a broadening.  An increase in the number of years allowed for both
35:1101:91240:12:12:63:542:450:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:loss carryforward and loss carryback corresponds to a narrowing of the base, while a decrease corresponds to a broadening.  For
35:1102:91367:12:12:63:542:438:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:franchise taxes, federal income tax deductibility, federal accelerated depreciation and ACRS depreciation, the rule being turned
35:1103:91495:12:12:63:542:426:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:off corresponds to a narrowing of the base, while it being turned on corresponds to a narrowing.  For instance, if a state adopts
35:1104:91624:12:12:63:542:414:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:MACRS depreciation, then we say that the tax base has narrowed.  For throwback rules, combined reporting, moving average base
35:1105:91749:12:11:63:542:402:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:for incremental R&D, fixed base for incremental R&D and federal income as state tax base, the rule being turned off corresponds to
35:1106:91879:11:12:63:542:391:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:a narrowing of the base, while it being turned on corresponds to a broadening.  For instance, if a state adopts combined reporting,
35:1107:92010:12:12:63:542:379:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:then we say that the tax base has broadened.  If that state gets rid of combined reporting, then the tax base has narrowed.  See
35:1108:92138:12:12:63:542:367:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:Section 1 for details on data sources, and Appendix A for definitions of broadening and narrowing for each measure.  Appendix

38:1243:98689:12:12:63:542:166:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:taxes that depend on the structure of the state corporate tax system result in inconsistent estimates of the average partial effect
38:1244:98820:12:0:63:223:154:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:of taxes on revenues and economic activity.

42:1359:104222:0:19:63:545:724:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:F:A.2    Definitions of Broadening/Narrowing and Expected Sign of Interaction Terms
42:1360:104303:19:12:63:542:705:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:In  Tables2-  4  and  Appendix  TableA3we  analyze  changes  in  base  rules  and  code  changes  as  narrowing  or
42:1361:104418:12:12:63:542:693:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:broadening.  This definition also maps into expected signs for the interaction between taxes and base controls
42:1362:104528:12:20:63:168:681:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:in equation5 as follows:
42:1363:104552:20:19:78:476:661:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Throwback Rules:  “no” to “yes” is base broadening.  Expected interaction sign:  positive.
42:1364:104643:19:20:78:518:642:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Combined Reporting Rules:  “no” to “yes” is base broadening.  Expected interaction sign:  positive.
42:1365:104743:20:20:78:512:622:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Investment Tax Credit:  increase in credit is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1366:104844:20:12:78:542:602:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Research and Development Tax Credit:  increase in credit is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:
42:1367:104948:12:20:88:127:590:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:negative.
42:1368:104957:20:12:78:542:570:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Incremental R&D Credit, Base is Moving Average: “no” to “yes” is base broadening. Expected interaction
42:1369:105060:12:20:88:149:558:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:sign:  positive.
42:1370:105076:20:12:78:542:538:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Incremental R&D Credit, Base is Fixed:  “no” to “yes” is base broadening.  Expected interaction sign:
42:1371:105178:12:20:88:124:526:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:positive.
42:1372:105187:20:20:78:505:506:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Loss Carryback Rules:  increase in years is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1373:105286:20:20:78:518:486:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Loss Carryforward Rules:  increase in years is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1374:105388:20:20:78:509:466:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Franchise Tax (indicator):  “no” to “yes” is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1375:105488:20:12:78:542:446:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Federal  Income  Tax  Deductible:   “no”  to  “yes”  is  base  narrowing,  “yes”  to  “no”  is  base  broadening.
42:1376:105602:12:20:88:245:434:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1377:105639:20:12:78:542:414:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Federal Income as State Tax Base:  “no” to “yes” is base broadening, “yes” to “no” is base narrowing.
42:1378:105741:12:19:88:243:402:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:Expected interaction sign:  positive.
42:1379:105778:19:20:78:542:383:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Federal Accelerated Depreciation:  “no” to “yes” is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1380:105885:20:12:78:542:363:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Accelerated  Cost  Recovery  System  (ACRS)  Depreciation:  “no”  to  “yes”  is  base  narrowing.   Expected
42:1381:105994:12:20:88:201:351:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:interaction sign:  negative.
42:1382:106022:20:20:78:518:331:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Federal Bonus Depreciation:  “no” to “yes” is base narrowing.  Expected interaction sign:  negative.
42:1383:106123:20:12:78:542:311:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Sales  Apportionment  Weight:   increase  in  sales  weight  is  base  narrowing.   Expected  interaction  sign:
42:1384:106236:12:28:88:127:299:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:negative.
42:1385:106245:28:18:63:229:271:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:A.3    R&D Tax Credit Base
42:1386:106271:18:12:63:542:253:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:The effective R&D tax credit rate is a combination of 3 factors:  the statutory R&D tax credit rate, the base
42:1387:106380:12:12:63:542:241:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:level definition, and the recapture policy (Wilson,2005).  States vary in the definition of the applicable base
42:1388:106491:12:22:63:495:229:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:for R&D tax credits.  As pointed out inWilson(2009), such definitions fall into 3 major categories:
42:1389:106590:22:20:75:403:207:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:1.Non-incremental credit:  all R&D expenditures are eligible for credit.
42:1390:106662:20:12:75:542:187:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:2.Incremental credit with a moving average base:  only R&D expenditures above a base level deter-
42:1391:106759:12:12:88:542:175:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:mined by the firm’srecentactivity are eligible for credit.  This base level is usually a moving average of
42:1392:106865:12:20:88:328:163:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:the firm’s R&D over the past 1-4 years (Wilson,2005).
42:1393:106918:20:12:75:542:143:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:3.Incremental credit with a fixed-period base: only R&D expenditures above a base level determined
42:1394:107016:12:0:88:390:131:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:?:by the firm’s activityduring a fixed past periodare eligible for credit.
43:1395:107090:0:12:78:542:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:From 1980-2010, several states rely on the federal definition of the base level.  The federal definition used a
43:1396:107201:12:12:63:542:712:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:3-year moving average until 1989, which was computed as the multiplication of current sales and the average
43:1397:107308:12:12:63:542:700:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:R&D-to-sales  ratio  over  the  past  3  years  (Wilson(2009);Chang(2014);Rao(2016)).   With  the  passage
43:1398:107414:12:12:63:542:688:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of  Public  Law  101-239  on  December  19,  1989,  the  federal  R&D  regime  shifted  to  a  fixed-period  base  level
43:1399:107534:12:12:63:542:676:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:definition  (Chang,2014).   Under  this  regime,  the  base  level  is  computed  as  a  firm’s  recent  sales  times  the
43:1400:107656:12:12:63:543:664:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:average  R&D-sales  ratio  over  the  period  1984-1988  (Wilson,2005).   In  addition,  states  have  set  their  own
43:1401:107774:12:12:63:542:652:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:definitions of the R&D tax base.  To account for the effects of different R&D tax credit regimes on state tax
43:1402:107883:12:12:63:542:640:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:revenues and economic activity,  we control for two indicators of the type of incremental base a state might
43:1403:107991:12:28:63:469:628:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:have:  fixed or moving average.  We use data fromWilson(2009) to generate these indicators.
43:1404:108082:28:18:63:230:600:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:A.4    Bartik Tax Base Rules
43:1405:108110:18:20:75:152:582:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:1.  Property taxes
43:1406:108128:20:16:100:205:562:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Variable:  propertytax
43:1407:108151:16:16:100:205:546:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Source:Bartik(2017)
43:1408:108171:16:12:100:542:530:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Definition:   Real  property  tax  rate  for  industrial  real  property,  industrial  machinery  and  equip-
43:1409:108281:12:12:110:542:518:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:ment,  and  industrial  inventories.   Real  property  includes  both  land  and  buildings.   For  all  non-
43:1410:108390:12:12:110:542:506:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:manufacturing industries, the commercial tax rates are applied.  The tax rates are applied to real
43:1411:108488:12:12:110:542:494:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:property,  and  to  personal  property  excluding  inventories.   Inventories  are  assumed  to  always  be
43:1412:108595:12:12:110:542:482:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:exempt.  The tax rates were interpolated for missing years, assuming the tax rate changes linearly
43:1413:108693:12:20:110:235:470:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:between the two years given.
43:1414:108721:20:20:75:193:450:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:2.  Property tax abatement
43:1415:108747:20:16:100:219:430:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Variable:  propabatement
43:1416:108772:16:16:100:205:414:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Source:Bartik(2017)
43:1417:108792:16:11:100:542:398:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Definition:  The nominal value of the property tax abatement rate for each city under consideration
43:1418:108892:11:12:110:542:387:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:inBartik(2017).  The database inBartik(2017) seeks to determine not just what the state allows
43:1419:108986:12:20:110:352:375:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:in property tax abatements, but what specific cities do.
43:1420:109042:20:20:75:191:355:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:3.  Job creation tax credits
43:1421:109070:20:16:100:220:335:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Variable:  jobcreationcred
43:1422:109097:16:16:100:205:319:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Source:Bartik(2017)
43:1423:109117:16:12:100:542:303:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f4:A:•Definition:  The nominal value of the job creation tax credit, calculated before considering any limits
43:1424:109221:12:0:110:186:291:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:on the tax credit.
44:1425:109241:0:24:63:407:724:14:g_d0_f14:14:g_d0_f14:C:B    Construction of Neighbor and Similar States
44:1426:109289:24:19:63:209:700:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:B.1    Neighboring States
44:1427:109314:19:11:63:542:681:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Neighbor states are states that share a border of any length. There exist 109 unique state border pairs, including
44:1428:109428:11:12:63:542:670:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:pairs sharing a single-point border.  States with no interstate border are not included in the sample.  We draw
44:1429:109539:12:12:63:542:658:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:our border data from Holmes (1998).  It includes 48 states (Alaska and Hawaii share no borders with other US
44:1430:109647:12:12:63:542:646:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:states).  The District of Columbia is excluded from our sample.  We then construct a dataset with 218 state
44:1431:109754:12:12:63:542:634:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:border pairs such that for each bordering statesiandj,  we have the state pairijandji.  We then merge
44:1432:109855:12:28:63:483:622:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:corporate tax rate and base measure data for each stateiand bordering statejfrom 1980-2010.
44:1433:109946:28:19:63:179:594:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:B.2    Similar States
44:1434:109967:19:12:63:542:575:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:We use state-level demographic and economic characteristics to construct a measure of state similarity.  For
44:1435:110075:12:11:63:542:563:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f10:B:each stateiand yeartin our sample, we fit a logistic regression to estimate the probability that statej6=i
44:1436:110181:11:12:63:542:552:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:is stateiin yeart.  The estimates from this regression provide a measure of how similar states are to a given
44:1437:110290:12:12:63:154:540:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:state in a given year.
44:1438:110312:12:22:78:346:528:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:Specifically, for each state-year, we estimate the specification:
44:1439:110377:22:15:137:468:506:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f11:?:Prob(j=i)jt=β0+β1manufjt+β2servicejt+β3agrjt+β4constrminejt
44:1440:110436:15:22:221:542:491:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:+β5skilljt+β6log(pop)jt+εjt(9)
44:1441:110466:22:12:63:543:469:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:whereProb(j=i)  is  the  probability  that  statejis  statei;manufis  manufacturing  share  of  state  GDP;
44:1442:110573:12:12:63:542:457:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f4:B:serviceis information and professional services’ share of state GDP;agris agriculture, forestry, fishing and
44:1443:110681:12:12:63:542:445:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:hunting share of state GDP;constrmineis construction, mining and utilities share of state GDP;skillis the
44:1444:110786:12:12:63:542:433:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:share of the state population over 18 with a Bachelor’s Degree or above; and log(pop) is log state population in
44:1445:110898:12:12:63:542:421:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:yeart.  Appendix TableA13summarizes the covariates used to construct the similarity index.  Industry share
44:1446:111004:12:12:63:542:409:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:of GDP was measured by the Bureau of Economic Analysis.  We then calculate the “distance” betweenjand
44:1447:111105:12:12:63:542:397:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f5:F:i, defined asdij= [LProb(i=j)−LProb(i=i)]2, or the squared difference between the linear probabilities.36
44:1448:111210:12:12:63:542:385:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Statei’s “similar” state in yeartis the state whose estimated probability yields the smallestdijin yeart−1.
44:1449:111317:12:12:78:542:373:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:A  key  difference  between  identifying  border  and  similar  states  is  that  state  similarity  is  not  necessarily
44:1450:111438:12:12:63:542:361:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:reciprocal.  In other words, Maine may be similar to Vermont in yeart, but Vermont is not necessarily similar
44:1451:111547:12:12:63:105:349:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:to Maine.
44:1452:111556:12:12:78:542:337:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:One  shortcoming  of  this  method  is  that  it  does  not  identify  similar  matches  for  all  states  in  all  years.
44:1453:111678:12:12:63:542:325:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Only 25 states have a “similar” state for every sample year; the other 25 are missing matches in some or all
44:1454:111786:12:12:63:542:313:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:sample years.  The reason is that some states are too economically different from the rest of the nation.  For
44:1455:111896:12:11:63:542:301:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:example, California has no matches because it is exactly identified by its population, and the probability that
44:1456:112007:11:12:63:542:290:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:any other state is California is infinitely close to 0.37Appendix TableA14lists all states in our sample and
44:1457:112115:12:12:63:542:278:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:their “similar” states in the year before a tax rate or base change.  We hold the “similar” state constant in the
44:1458:112228:12:12:63:543:266:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:years surrounding an event when estimating the results of Appendix TablesA5andA6, and Appendix Figure
44:1459:112329:12:28:63:83:254:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:A29.
44:1460:112333:28:19:63:481:226:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:B.3    Estimating Event Probability Subject to Events in Similar States
44:1461:112404:19:12:63:542:207:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:Appendix TablesA5andA6describe how the probability of a corporate tax rate or base change is affected by
44:1462:112508:12:12:63:542:195:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:events in states’ neighbors and economically similar counterparts.  LetYitindicate a corporate rate increase or
44:1463:112619:12:11:63:542:183:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:decrease, or broadening or narrowing of the tax base in stateiand yeart.  Denote the set of neighbors and
44:1464:112724:11:15:63:542:172:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:similar statesj6=i.  The results in Appendix TableA5are estimated by running a probit regression of the
44:1465:112827:15:13:73:521:157:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:36We estimate the Hosmer-Lemeshow statistic for each logistic regression, and fail to reject the null that the indicator of
44:1466:112950:13:9:63:528:144:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:wether any state is stateiis orthogonal to the covariates listed in equation 9.  This suggests that the matching regression has
44:1467:113077:9:7:63:145:135:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:high predictive power.
44:1468:113099:7:12:73:535:128:6:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f8:A:37We explored using OLS to avoid these issues when estimatingProb(j=i)jt, but this approach can yield predicted proba-
44:1469:113217:12:0:63:239:116:8:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f8:F:bilities that fall outside the range of 0 to 100%.
45:1470:113269:0:22:63:86:724:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:form:
45:1471:113274:22:15:141:396:702:10:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f5:?:P(Yit= 1) =β0+β1D[RateInc]j,t−1+β2D[RateDec]j,t−1
45:1472:113323:15:22:212:542:687:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:+β3D[BaseNarrow]j,t−1+β3D[BaseBroaden]j,t−1+εit(10)
45:1473:113374:22:22:63:400:665:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:while the results in Appendix TableA6are estimated by similarly estimating
45:1474:113448:22:15:148:388:643:10:g_d0_f10:5:g_d0_f28:?:P(Yit= 1) =β0+β1D[RateInc]j,t′+β2D[RateDec]j,t′
45:1475:113495:15:22:220:542:628:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:+β3D[BaseNarrow]j,t′+β3D[BaseBroaden]j,t′+εit(11)
45:1476:113544:22:12:63:165:606:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:wheret′∈[t−5,t−1].
45:1477:113562:12:12:78:542:594:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:A:In the neighbor states case, we consider changes in corporate tax rate and in tax base that took place in
45:1478:113667:12:12:63:542:582:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:any ofi’s border states.  For example, the indicator for whether a corporate rate increase took place in Maine’s
45:1479:113779:12:12:63:542:570:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:neighboring states in the previous year equals 1 if Vermont’s corporate tax rate increased in yeart−1.  We
45:1480:113885:12:12:63:542:558:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:present results fork= 1, i.e., a neighbor changed rates last year, andk∈[1,5], i.e., if an event occurred at
45:1481:113993:12:0:63:221:546:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:B:least once in the previous five years.
